Coercion and Consuming Forbidden Substances
Ruling with proof on coercion and consumption of forbidden substances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish compelling coercion (ikrah mulji') from non-compelling coercion, state the Hanafi ruling on consuming forbidden substances under each, and explain the evidence from Quran 6:119 and the intra-Hanafi dispute over sin for refusal under life-threatening coercion.

Core Idea
Under life-threatening coercion, the forbidden becomes permissible; refusing and being killed is sinful, contrary to Abu Yusuf's view.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on consuming forbidden substances such as carrion, pork, blood, and wine when one is coerced. The key distinction is between compelling coercion that threatens life or limb and lesser forms of coercion. We will explore the primary evidence from the Quran, the conditions for permissibility, and an important intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether refraining is sinful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the coercion level
First, determine the specific prohibited act (eating carrion, pork, drinking wine) and the nature of the coercion described in the text: is it threat of death or amputation, or merely beating, imprisonment, or shackling?
The matn states: 'with killing or amputation it is permissible' (حل بقتل وقطع).
2
Apply the Hanafi rule of necessity
Use the principle that prohibition is restricted to the state of choice (hāl al-ikhtiyār). Under necessity (idtirār), the original permissibility of these substances returns, based on Quran 6:119.
The exception (istithnā') in the verse covers only genuine necessity.
3
Define compelling coercion (ikrah mulji')
Determine how the authors define 'fear for life or limb'. The passage states it is not achieved by beating alone, imprisonment, or sound; it requires a genuine belief that death or loss of limb will occur.
The author criticizes fixing a specific number of lashes; it depends on the individual's condition.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on sin
The majority (Abū Ḥanīfa and Muḥammad) hold that if one refuses under compelling coercion and is killed, he sins because he refrained from a permissible act. Abū Yūsuf holds he does not sin, considering refraining the stronger position (azīma).
The commentator sides with the majority, arguing that necessity makes compliance obligatory, not merely permissible.
5
Determine the operative ruling (muftā bihi)
Conclude that the relied-upon position is the majority view: it is permissible—and even obligatory—to consume under compelling coercion, and refusal leading to death is sinful.
The hadd punishment for drinking wine under coercion is averted due to shubha (semblance of permissibility).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وعلى أكل لحم خنزير وميتة ودم وشرب خمر يحبس أو ضرب أو قيد لم يحل وحل بقتل وقطع) يعني لو أكره على هذه الأشياء بما لا يخاف على نفسه أو عضوه كالضرب لا يسعه أن يقدم عليه وبما يخاف يسعه ذلك لأن حرمة هذه الأشياء مقيدة بحالة الاختيار وفي حالة الضرورة مبقات على أصل الحل لقوله تعالى وإلا ما اضطررتم إليه ﴾ [الأنعام: ۱۱۹] فاستثنى حالة الاضطرار لأنه فيها مباح والاضطرار يحصل بالإكراه الملجئ وهو أن يخاف على نفسه أو عضوه ولا يحصل ذلك بالضرب بالصوت ولا بالحبس حتى لو خاف ذلك منه وغلب على ظنه يباح له ذلك. أقول : في قوله يباح له ذلك إشكال قوي فإن المباح ما استوى طرفاه فعله وتركه كما تقرر في علم الأصول، وفيما نحن فيه إذا خيف على النفس أو على عضو كان طرف العقل راجحاً بل فرضاً كما صرح به في لب الأصول من كون ذلك فرضاً فتأمل فلو قال بغير ما يخاف منه على تلف عضو أو نفسه لم يفترض وإلا افترض إلى آخره لكان أولى. وقدره بعضهم بأدنى وهو أربعون سوطاً فإن هدد به وسعه أن يقدم وإن هدد بدونه لا يسعه لأنه ما دون ذلك مشروع بطريق التعزير . قلنا لا وجه للتعزير بالرأي وأحوال الناس مختلفة فمنهم من يحمل الضرب الشديد ومنهم من يموت بأدنى منه فلا طريق سوى الرجوع إلى رأي المبتلى، فإن غلب على ظنه أن تلف النفس أو العضو يحصل به وسعه وإلا فلا، وإذا قلنا لا شرب الخمر هل يحد أم لا ؟ قال في المحيط : وإذا شرب الخمر لا يحد لأن بأغلظ إلاكراهين تثبت حقيقة إباحة الشرب حالة الضرورة وبأخفهما ثبت شبهة الإباحة والشبهة كافية لدرء الحدود اهـ. وفي المبسوط : الإكراه على المعاصي أنواع : نوع يرخص له فعله ويثاب على تركه، وقسم حرام فعله مأثوم على إتيانه، وقسم يباح فعله ويأثم على تركه الأول الإكراه على إجراء كلمة الكفر وشتم محمد هو أو على ترك الصلاة أو كل ما ثبت بالكتاب. الثاني كما لو أكره بالقتل على أن يقتل مسلماً أو يقطع عضوه أو يضربه ضرباً يخاف منه التلف أو مسلماً أو يؤذيه أو على الزنا. والثالث لو أكره على الخمر وما ذكر معه. قال رحمه الله : (وأثم بصيره) يعني إذا أكره على ما تقدم بقتل وقطع فلم يفعل حتى قتله أو قطع عضواً منه أثم لأن التناول في هذه الحالة مباح وإتلاف النفس أو العضو بالامتناع عن المباح حرام فيأثم إلا أنه إذا لم يعلم الإباحة في هذه الحالة لا يأثم لأنه موضع الخفاء وقد دخله اختلاف العلماء فلا يأثم كالجهل بالخطاب في دار الحرب أو في أول الإسلام في حق من أسلم فيها. وعن أبي يوسف لا يأثم مطلقاً لأنه رخصة إذ الحرمة قائمة فيكون أخذا بالعزيمة. قلنا: حالة الاضطرار مستثناة فلا يكون الامتناع عزيمة بل معصية. قال في العناية : فإن قيل : إضافة الإثم إلى ترك المباح من باب فساد الوضع وهو فاسد فالجواب أن المباح إنما يجوز تركه يشتم يسعه
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And regarding eating pork, carrion, blood, and drinking wine, being imprisoned, beaten, or shackled, it is not permissible, but with killing or amputation it is permissible.' Meaning, if one is coerced into these things by something that does not cause fear for his life or limb, like beating, it is not permissible for him to do them. But by something that causes fear, it is permissible for him, because the prohibition of these things is restricted to the state of choice, and in a state of necessity it reverts to the original permissibility, due to His statement: 'except what you are compelled to' [Al-An'am 6:119]. He exempted the state of necessity because in it it is permissible. Necessity arises from compelling coercion (ikrah mulji'), which is fear for one's life or limb. It does not arise from beating with a sound or imprisonment. So if he fears that from him and it becomes his predominant belief, it becomes permissible for him. I say: In his saying 'it is permissible for him' there is a strong problem. For the permissible is that whose two sides are equal – doing it and leaving it – as established in usul al-fiqh. In our case, when one fears for life or limb, the side of reason is preponderant, rather it is obligatory, as stated in Lub al-Usul that it is obligatory. So ponder. It would have been better if he said 'without what he fears from loss of limb or life, it is not obligatory; otherwise it is obligatory' etc. Some have estimated the minimum as forty lashes. If threatened with that, he may do it; if threatened with less, it is not permissible, because less than that is prescribed as ta'zir. We say: There is no basis for ta'zir by opinion, and people's conditions differ. Some bear severe beating; others die from the least. There is no way except referring to the opinion of the person tested. If it is his predominant belief that loss of life or limb will occur from it, he may do it; otherwise not. And if we say he does not drink wine, is the hadd punishment imposed or not? He said in al-Muhit: If he drinks wine, the hadd is not imposed, because with the stronger of the two forms of coercion the actual permissibility of drinking is established in necessity, and with the lighter a semblance (shubha) of permissibility is established, and the semblance is sufficient to avert the hadd punishments. In al-Mabsut: Coercion into sins is of types: one type is that it is permitted for him to do it and he is rewarded for refraining; a second type is that doing it is forbidden and he sins by doing it; a third type is that doing it is permissible and he sins by refraining. The first is coercion to utter words of disbelief, insulting Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, or to abandon prayer, or anything established by the Book. The second is like being coerced by threat of death to kill a Muslim, or amputate his limb, or beat him with a blow that one fears will be lethal, or to harm a Muslim, or to commit zina. The third is coercion to drink wine and what was mentioned with it. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And he sins by his sight' meaning if he is coerced into the aforementioned by threat of killing or amputation, and he does not do it until the threatening person kills him or amputates a limb, he sins because consumption in this situation is permissible, and destroying life or limb by refraining from the permissible is forbidden, so he sins. However, if he does not know the permissibility in this situation, he does not sin because it is a concealed matter in which scholars have differed, so he does not sin like ignorance of the address in dar al-harb or in early Islam for one who accepted Islam there. From Abu Yusuf: He does not sin at all, because it is a concession; the prohibition remains, so refraining is adhering to the stronger (azima). We say: The state of necessity is exempted, so refraining is not azima but disobedience. In al-ʿInaya: If it is said: Attaching sin to refraining from the permissible is a corrupt construction, and it is corrupt, the answer is that the permissible is only permitted to be refrained from... [text unclear].
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the fiqh of coercion (ikrah) regarding consuming forbidden substances like pork, carrion, blood, and wine. The author explains the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq: if coercion involves only beating, imprisonment, or shackling (i.e., non-life-threatening) it is not permissible to consume these; but if it involves threats of killing or amputation (life-threatening), it becomes permissible. The basis is Quran 6:119, which exempts necessity from the prohibition. Necessity here is defined as 'ikrah mulji'' – compelling coercion where one fears for life or limb. The author raises an objection: normally 'mubah' means doing and leaving are equal, but here leaving is actually obligatory (fard) because one is required to preserve life. He suggests the matn should have distinguished between obligatory and non-obligatory cases. The text then discusses the minimum threat: some scholars say 40 lashes; but the author rejects quantification, saying it depends on the individual's fear. As for hadd punishment for drinking wine under coercion: the hadd is averted because there is a shubha (semblance) of permissibility. The passage then categorizes coercion into sins: (1) coercion into kufr or abandoning obligations – it is permitted to comply; (2) coercion into harming a Muslim or zina – it is forbidden to comply even under threat of death; (3) coercion into consuming wine etc. – it is permissible to comply, and one sins if he refuses and is killed. Regarding sin: if one refuses under life-threatening coercion and is killed, he sins because he refrained from a permissible act, which becomes haram. However, if he is ignorant of the rule, there is no sin due to the difference of scholars. Abu Yusuf holds that he does not sin at all because refraining is the azima. The author rejects this, insisting necessity makes compliance obligatory.

Key Terms
الإكراه الملجئ (al-ikrāh al-muljiʾ): Compelling coercion that threatens life or limb, causing fear of death or severe harm.
الاضطرار (al-iḍṭirār): Necessity, a situation where one is forced by fear of death or harm to violate a prohibition.
الحدود (al-ḥudūd): Fixed punishments prescribed by Shariah for certain crimes, such as drinking wine (hadd al-shurb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a person coerced with threat of death to drink wine?
A) It is permissible to drink, and if he refuses and is killed he sins.
B) It is permissible to drink, and if he refuses he is rewarded.
C) It remains haram and he must not drink even if killed.
D) It is obligatory to drink but he does not sin if he refuses.

Key Takeaway
Only life-threatening coercion (ikrah mulji') lifts the prohibition on forbidden substances; refusal leading to death is sinful according to the majority Hanafi view.

Valid Cutting Instruments: Detached vs Attached Nail and Tooth
Ruling with explanation on valid cutting instruments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a detached versus attached nail or tooth for slaughter and explain why attached ones are invalid (cutting by weight, not sharpness).

Core Idea
A detached nail or tooth is a valid cutting instrument; an attached one is not because it cuts by weight.

The first part of the passage establishes a key condition for the slaughtering instrument: it must cut by its sharpness, not by crushing or weight. A detached nail or tooth qualifies because it can be sharpened and cuts like a knife, but an attached nail or tooth cannot cut properly; it merely crushes by the weight of the hand, rendering the slaughter invalid. This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school and emphasizes the importance of the tool's function over its form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on detached nail/tooth
The text explicitly states that the detached nail and tooth are valid cutting instruments (ālah jāriḥah). Detached means separated from the body, so a fallen fingernail or extracted tooth can be used.
2
Understand the rationale for attached nail/tooth
The attached nail or tooth is not valid because slaughter with it relies on weight (al-thiqal) rather than the cutting action of the instrument. The tool must cut by its sharpness, not by pressing down.
This rationale is based on the definition of 'cutting instrument'.
3
Apply the distinction to practice
If a person slaughters with an attached fingernail or tooth, the slaughter is invalid and the animal is not halal. If they use a detached nail or tooth, it is valid provided it is sharp enough to cut.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school differs: they hold that a nail (detached or attached) is never valid for slaughter, while a tooth is valid only if detached. The Hanafi view is more permissive regarding detached nails.
This comparison highlights the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والظفر والسن المنزوع آلة جارحة بخلاف غير المنزوع لأن الذبح به يكون بالثقل لا بالآلة اهـ . قال رحمه الله : ( وندب حد شفرته لقوله عليه الصلاة إن الله كتب الإحسان على كل شيء فإذا قتلتم فأحسنوا القتلة وإذا ذبحتم فأحسنوا الذبحة وليحد أحدكم شفرته وليرح ذبيحته» رواه مسلم وغيره ويكره أن يضجعها ثم يحد الشفرة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لمن أضجع الشاة وهو يحد شفرته لقد أردت أن تميتها موتتين هلا حددتها قبل أن تضجعها الحديث والآلة على ضربين : قاطعة وغير قاطعة والقاطعة على ضربين : حادة وكليلة ؛ فالحادة اختيارية وضرورية، فالحادة يجوز الذبح بها من غير كراهة والكليلة يجوز الذبح بها ويكره لما مر من الإبطاء في الإراقة؛ كذا في المحيط .
And the detached nail and tooth are a cutting instrument, unlike the attached [nail and tooth] because slaughter with it [the attached] is by weight, not by the instrument. End. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is recommended to sharpen his blade because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed excellence in everything. So when you kill, kill well; and when you slaughter, slaughter well. Let one of you sharpen his blade and let him give rest to his sacrificial animal.') Reported by Muslim and others. And it is disliked to lay it down then sharpen the blade because of his saying, peace be upon him, to one who laid down the sheep while sharpening his blade: 'You intended to kill it twice; why did you not sharpen it before laying it down?' The hadith. And the instrument is of two types: cutting and non-cutting. The cutting is of two types: sharp and dull. The sharp is optional and necessary; slaughter with the sharp is permissible without dislike, and with the dull it is permissible but disliked due to the slowness in blood flow mentioned earlier. This is from al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement with proof. The passage first clarifies that a detached nail or tooth (i.e., removed from the body) is considered a valid cutting instrument, whereas an attached nail or tooth is not because slaughter with it relies on weight rather than a true cutting action. This distinction is crucial: for slaughter to be valid, the tool must cut by its sharpness, not by crushing. The author then quotes the matn recommending the sharpening of the blade, supported by a hadith from Muslim commanding excellence in slaughter. The hadith emphasizes sharpening the blade and giving the animal rest to minimize suffering. It also warns against laying the animal down before sharpening, as that causes unnecessary pain. Finally, instruments are categorized: cutting (sharp or dull) and non-cutting. A sharp blade is recommended and permissible without dislike; a dull blade is permissible but disliked because it delays blood flow, causing more suffering.

Key Terms
آلة جارحة (ālah jāriḥah): A cutting instrument that cuts by its sharpness, such as a knife, as opposed to a crushing instrument.
الظفر (al-ẓufr): The fingernail or toenail, which when detached is considered a valid cutting instrument.
السن (al-sinn): The tooth, which when detached is considered a valid cutting instrument.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, why is an attached tooth invalid for slaughter?
A) It is impure.
B) It is not sharp enough.
C) It cuts by weight, not by sharpness.
D) It is too small.

Key Takeaway
A detached nail or tooth is a valid cutting instrument because it cuts by sharpness; an attached one is invalid because it relies on weight.

Recommendation to Sharpen the Blade and Classification of Instruments
Ruling with proof on recommended actions and instrument classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on sharpening the blade before slaughter (sunnah muakkadah), identify the disliked actions, and classify instruments into sharp (no dislike), dull (disliked), and non-cutting (invalid).

Core Idea
Sharpening the blade is a sunnah muakkadah; sharpening after laying the animal down is disliked.

The second part of the passage focuses on the etiquette and legal categories of the slaughtering instrument. The author quotes the well-known hadith commanding excellence in slaughter, which includes sharpening the blade and giving rest to the animal. The Hanafi school interprets the command as a strong recommendation (sunnah muakkadah), not an obligation. Additionally, a separate hadith forbids sharpening the blade after the animal is laid down, making that action disliked. Finally, instruments are divided into cutting (qāṭiʿah) and non-cutting; cutting instruments are further divided into sharp (ḥāddah) – which is preferred – and dull (kalīlah) – which is permissible but disliked due to slow blood flow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah of sharpening
The text states 'it is recommended to sharpen his blade' (undub ḥadd shafratihi). This is a sunnah muakkadah based on the prophetic command.
2
Analyze the dalil
The hadith from Muslim uses the imperative 'ليحد' (let him sharpen). According to Hanafi usul, an imperative in the context of slaughter indicates recommendation (nadb) because a dull blade is still permissible, so the command is not for obligation.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalālah.
3
Understand the prohibition of sharpening after laying the animal down
Another hadith rebukes a man who sharpened his knife after laying the sheep down, saying 'you intended to kill it twice'. This makes the action makruh tanzihan (disliked) because it causes unnecessary suffering.
4
Classify instruments
The passage categorizes instruments into: (1) non-cutting (invalid), (2) cutting: (a) sharp – permissible without dislike, (b) dull – permissible but disliked. Sharp is further divided into optional and necessary? The text says 'al-ḥāddah ikhtiyāriyyah wa ḍarūriyyah' meaning sharp is both optional (when available) and necessary (when available?) but the meaning is ambiguous; the commentator explains that sharp is always preferable.
The classification helps determine the ruling: sharp is best, dull is permissible but makruh.

Source Text

والظفر والسن المنزوع آلة جارحة بخلاف غير المنزوع لأن الذبح به يكون بالثقل لا بالآلة اهـ . قال رحمه الله : ( وندب حد شفرته لقوله عليه الصلاة إن الله كتب الإحسان على كل شيء فإذا قتلتم فأحسنوا القتلة وإذا ذبحتم فأحسنوا الذبحة وليحد أحدكم شفرته وليرح ذبيحته» رواه مسلم وغيره ويكره أن يضجعها ثم يحد الشفرة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لمن أضجع الشاة وهو يحد شفرته لقد أردت أن تميتها موتتين هلا حددتها قبل أن تضجعها الحديث والآلة على ضربين : قاطعة وغير قاطعة والقاطعة على ضربين : حادة وكليلة ؛ فالحادة اختيارية وضرورية، فالحادة يجوز الذبح بها من غير كراهة والكليلة يجوز الذبح بها ويكره لما مر من الإبطاء في الإراقة؛ كذا في المحيط .
And the detached nail and tooth are a cutting instrument, unlike the attached [nail and tooth] because slaughter with it [the attached] is by weight, not by the instrument. End. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is recommended to sharpen his blade because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed excellence in everything. So when you kill, kill well; and when you slaughter, slaughter well. Let one of you sharpen his blade and let him give rest to his sacrificial animal.') Reported by Muslim and others. And it is disliked to lay it down then sharpen the blade because of his saying, peace be upon him, to one who laid down the sheep while sharpening his blade: 'You intended to kill it twice; why did you not sharpen it before laying it down?' The hadith. And the instrument is of two types: cutting and non-cutting. The cutting is of two types: sharp and dull. The sharp is optional and necessary; slaughter with the sharp is permissible without dislike, and with the dull it is permissible but disliked due to the slowness in blood flow mentioned earlier. This is from al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement with proof. The passage first clarifies that a detached nail or tooth (i.e., removed from the body) is considered a valid cutting instrument, whereas an attached nail or tooth is not because slaughter with it relies on weight rather than a true cutting action. This distinction is crucial: for slaughter to be valid, the tool must cut by its sharpness, not by crushing. The author then quotes the matn recommending the sharpening of the blade, supported by a hadith from Muslim commanding excellence in slaughter. The hadith emphasizes sharpening the blade and giving the animal rest to minimize suffering. It also warns against laying the animal down before sharpening, as that causes unnecessary pain. Finally, instruments are categorized: cutting (sharp or dull) and non-cutting. A sharp blade is recommended and permissible without dislike; a dull blade is permissible but disliked because it delays blood flow, causing more suffering.

Key Terms
الشفرة (al-shafrah): The blade of the knife used for slaughter.
الإحسان في الذبح (al-iḥsān fī al-dhabh): Excellence in slaughter, including sharpening the blade, giving rest to the animal, and swift cutting.
الإبطاء في الإراقة (al-ibṭāʾ fī al-irāqah): Slowness in blood flow, which occurs with a dull blade and causes suffering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, slaughter with a dull blade is:
A) Invalid (batil).
B) Valid but disliked (makruh).
C) Valid and not disliked.
D) Prohibited (haram).

Key Takeaway
Sharpening the blade is a sunnah muakkadah; a dull blade is valid but disliked; sharpening after laying the animal down is also disliked.

Disliked Actions in Slaughter: When Carnality Meets Validity
Lists disliked actions in slaughter and their legal effect on meat permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the disliked actions in slaughter according to the Hanafi school and explain why the meat remains permissible despite these actions.

Core Idea
Disliked actions in slaughter increase pain but do not make meat haram unless the animal dies before proper throat cutting.

Slaughter (dhabh) in Islam is an act of worship with specific conditions. However, some actions, though disliked (makruh), do not invalidate the slaughter or render the meat impermissible. In this passage, the author lists several such actions—breaking the neck, cutting the head, slaughtering from the back—and explains their legal effect. Understanding the distinction between a disliked action and an invalid slaughter is key to correctly applying Hanafi fiqh in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disliked Actions
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. List the specific actions the author describes as disliked: al-nakh' (breaking/bending the neck), qat' al-ra's (cutting the head), and al-dhabh min al-qafa' (slaughtering from the back). Also note additional disliked acts: dragging the animal, skinning before it cools, and facing away from the qiblah.
The passage uses the verb 'kariha' (disliked) for each.
2
Understand the Reason for Dislike
The commentary explains that these actions are disliked because they cause additional unnecessary pain to the animal. The fundamental principle is that unnecessary suffering is discouraged, but as long as the essential conditions of valid slaughter are met, the meat remains halal.
The hadith cited prohibits 'nahn al-sha' (bending the neck) – this is the basis for the ruling.
3
Analyze the Effect on Meat Permissibility
The author explicitly states that despite the dislike, the meat is eaten (tu'kal) because the karahah is for an extra meaning (increased pain) and does not necessitate unlawfulness. However, a critical condition is attached: the animal must remain alive until the throat veins (awraq) are cut. If it dies before that, the meat becomes carrion.
This is the key legal distinction: the action is makruh, but the meat is halal, provided the slaughter itself is valid.
4
Recognize the Boundary Condition
The passage also covers the scenario when slaughter is done from the back: if the animal is still alive when the veins are cut, it is permissible; if it dies before, it is not. This shows that the timing of death relative to the cut is decisive, not the direction of the cut.
This is analogous to the general rule in Hanafi fiqh: the critical factor is the cutting of the veins while the animal is alive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وكره النخع وقطع الرأس والذبح من أن يصل إلى النخاع وهو خيط أبيض في جوف عظم القفاء) النخع هو الرقبة وهو بالفتح والضم لغة فيه. قال في النهاية ومن قال هو عرق أبيض فقدسها. واعترضه صاحب العناية أن من سمى بما ذكر لم يغلط لأن أهل اللغة ذكروه بلفظ الخيط وإنما كره لنهيه عليه الصلاة والسلام عن أن ننح الشاة إذا ذبحت وتفسيره ما ذكرنا. وقيل: أن يمد رأسها حتى يظهر مذبحها وقيل أن يكسر رقبتها قبل أن تسكن من الاضطراب وكل ذلك مكروه. وفي قطع الرأس زيادة تعذيب فيكره، ويكره أن يجر ما يريد ذبحه وأن يسلخ قبل أن يبرد ويؤكل في جميع ذلك لأن الكراهة لمعنى زائد وهو زيادة الألم فلا يوجب الحرمة. ويكره أن يذبحها موجهة لغير القبلة لمخالفة السنة في توجيهها للقبلة وتؤكل وفي الذبح من الفقا زيادة ألم فيكره، ويحل لما ذكرنا إذا بقيت حية حتى يقطع العروق لتحقق الموت بالذكاة، وإن ماتت قبل قطع العروق لا تؤكل لوجود الموت بما ليس بذكاة.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And he disliked breaking the neck (al-nakh'), cutting the head, and slaughtering from [the back] until [the knife] reaches the spinal cord (al-nukha'), which is a white thread inside the bone of the nape.) Al-nakh' is the neck, and it is pronounced with fatha and dammah as a linguistic variant. He said in al-Nihayah: And whoever said it is a white vein has erred. The author of al-Inayah objected that one who names it as mentioned does not err because the linguists mentioned it as a thread. And it is only disliked because of his prohibition, peace be upon him, against bending the sheep's neck when it has been slaughtered, and its interpretation is what we mentioned. And it is said: that he extends its head until its slaughter place appears. And it is said: that he breaks its neck before it becomes still from the agitation, and all of that is disliked. And in cutting off the head, there is additional torment, so it is disliked. And it is disliked to drag what he intends to slaughter, and to skin it before it cools down, and it is eaten in all of that because the dislike is for an additional meaning, which is increased pain, so it does not necessitate unlawfulness. And it is disliked to slaughter it facing other than the qiblah because it violates the sunnah of facing it towards the qiblah, and it is eaten. And in slaughter from the back (al-qafa), there is increased pain, so it is disliked; and it is rendered permissible, for what we mentioned, if it remains alive until the veins are cut to realize death by slaughter (dhabh). If it dies before the veins are cut, it is not eaten because death occurred by something other than slaughter.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement listing disliked acts in slaughter. The matn mentions three specific actions: (1) al-nakh' – breaking the neck (or spinal cord) after slaughter, (2) cutting off the head, and (3) slaughtering from the back until reaching the spinal cord. The commentary explains the linguistic meaning of nakh' and clarifies that it refers to bending or breaking the neck. All these actions are disliked (makruh tanzihi) because they cause unnecessary pain. The passage also notes that dragging the animal, skinning before it cools, and facing away from the qiblah are disliked. Importantly, despite being disliked, the meat remains permissible to eat because the karahah is only for an extra element of pain, not for a defect in the slaughter itself. However, if the animal dies from these actions before the throat veins are cut, it becomes carrion and is not permissible.

Key Terms
النخع (al-nakh'): Breaking or bending the neck after slaughter, which is disliked.
النخاع (al-nukha'): The spinal cord, a white thread inside the bone of the nape.
القفاء (al-qafā'): The back of the neck; slaughtering from this side is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person slaughters a sheep by cutting from the back of the neck (qafā') and the sheep dies before the throat veins are cut, what is the ruling?
A) The meat is halal because slaughter from the back is permissible.
B) The meat is not halal because death occurred without proper slaughter.
C) The meat is halal but the action is sinful.
D) The meat is halal only if the person intended to slaughter properly.

Key Takeaway
Disliked actions in slaughter do not affect the permissibility of the meat as long as the essential act of cutting the throat veins while the animal is alive has been performed.

The Principle of Jarh as Substitute for Slaughter
Determines when jarh is valid substitute for slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when wounding (jarh) is valid as a substitute for normal slaughter and identify the conditions required for the meat to be halal.

Core Idea
When normal slaughter is impossible, wounding becomes a valid method of tadhkiyah, provided the animal dies from the wound.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: what to do when an animal that is normally slaughtered becomes wild or falls into a well, making normal slaughter impossible. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: tame game must be slaughtered, but wild cattle or those that have fallen can be killed by wounding (jarh). We will explore the reasoning, conditions, and the prophetic proof that establishes this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The matn distinguishes between tame game (sayed musta'nis) and wild/fallen cattle (na'm tawahhasha aw taradda). State the ruling for each: tame game is slaughtered, wild/fallen cattle are killed by wounding.
2
Understand the condition of inability
The key factor is inability to perform normal slaughter (ajz). Why is this important? Because wounding only substitutes when normal slaughter is not possible.
3
Determine the cause of death
The meat is halal only if the animal died from the wound. If known to have died from another cause, it is haram. If uncertain, it is halal due to apparent cause.
4
Connect to the hadith proof
The hadith of the runaway camel demonstrates permissibility of shooting when normal slaughter is impossible. How does this prove the rule?
Hadith: 'Indeed these animals have wild instincts... so whatever they do, do to them like this.'
5
Apply to the aggressor (sa'il)
The ruling extends to any animal that attacks and cannot be caught, contrary to Malik. This shows the principle's breadth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وذبح صيد استأنس وجرح نعم توحش أو تردى في بئر) الواو عاطفة على قوله وحل ذبيحة مسلم وذبح صيد يعني وحل أكل صيد استأنس بالذبح وهو الاختيارية لقدرته عليها، وحل أكل نعم توحش أو تردى بالجرح لعجزه عن الاختيارية. هذا إذ علم أنه مات من الجرح، وإن علم أنه لم يمت من الجرح لم يؤكل» فإن أشكل ذلك أكل لأن الظاهر الموت به، وكذا الدجاجة إذا تعلقت على شجرة وخاف موتها صارت ذكاتها بالجرح وفي الكتاب أطلق فيما توحش من النعم وكذا فيما تردى فشمل ما إذا كان في المصر والصحراء، وعن محمد أن الشاة إذا ندت في المصر لا تحل بالعقر وإن ندت في الصحراء تحل بالعقر لتحقق العجز عن الذكاة الاختيارية وفي البقر والإبل يتحقق العجز سواء ندت في المصر أو في الصحراء فتحل بالعقر. والصائل كالناد إذا كان لا يقدر على أخذه حتى لو قتله المصول عليه وهو يريد ذكاته وسمى حل أكله خلافاً لمالك . ولنا ما روي منهم أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان في سفر فند بعير من الإبل ولم يكن معهم حبل فرماه رجل فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : إن لهذه البهائم أوابد كأوابد الوحش فما فعل منها فافعلوا به هكذا. رواه البخاري ومسلم ولأنه قد تحقق العجز عن الذكاة الاختيارية فصار إلى البدل. وفي النوازل : لو أن بقرة تعسر عليها الولادة فأدخل صاحبها يده وذبح الولد حل أكله، وإن جرحها في غير موضع الذبح إذا كان لا يقدر على ذبحه يحل وإن كان يقدر لا يحل اهـ. وفي المحيط : فإن أصاب قرنه أو ظفره أو حافره فإن أدماه ووصل للحم حل أكله وإلا فلا لأن الذكاة تصرف في محل الحياة وإن أبان عنه غير الرأس فمات يؤكل كله إلا ما أبان من الحي فهو ميت ولا يظهر فيه حكم الذكاة ولا كذلك إذا بان الرأس لأنه لا يتصور حياة الجسد مع إبانة الرأس. وإن تعلق منه جلدة فإن كان يلتئم ويتدبل لو تركه حل أكله وإلا فهو مبان، ولو قطع الصيد نصفين طولاً وعرضاً حل ولو أبان طائفة من الناس البدن إن كان أقل من النصف لا يحل المبان وإن كان النصف يصح كلاهما .اهـ.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the slaughter of game that has become tame, and the wounding of cattle that have become wild or have fallen into a well.) The waw is conjoined to his statement: 'And the permissible [consumption of] the slaughtered animal of a Muslim' and 'the slaughter of game' means: and the consumption of tame game is permissible by slaughter, which is the chosen method [of slaughter] due to ability over it; and the consumption of wild cattle or those that have fallen [into a well] is permissible by wounding due to inability to perform the chosen [slaughter]. This applies if it is known that it died from the wound; if it is known that it did not die from the wound, it is not eaten. If that is ambiguous, it is eaten because the apparent [state] is death by it. Similarly, if a chicken hangs on a tree and one fears its death, its slaughter [becomes] by wounding. In the book, he made it absolute regarding what has become wild from cattle, and similarly regarding what has fallen, so it includes whether it is in the city or the desert. From Muhammad: if a sheep runs away in the city, it is not permissible by shooting, but if it runs away in the desert, it is permissible by shooting due to the realization of inability to perform chosen slaughter. In cows and camels, inability is realized whether they run away in the city or the desert, so it is permissible by shooting. And the aggressor (al-sa'il) is like the runaway if one is unable to catch it; so if the aggressor kills it intending its slaughter and mentions [Allah's name], it is permissible to eat it, contrary to Malik. And we have [proof] from what was narrated from them: that he, peace be upon him, was on a journey, and a camel ran away, and they had no rope, so a man shot it. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed these animals have wild instincts like the wild beasts; so whatever they do, do to them like this.' Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. And because inability to perform chosen slaughter has been realized, so it resorts to the substitute. And in al-Nawazil: if a cow has difficulty giving birth, so its owner inserts his hand and slaughters the calf, it is permissible to eat it; and if he wounds it in a place other than the slaughter site, if he is unable to slaughter it, it is permissible; if he is able, it is not permissible. End. And in al-Muhit: if [a stray arrow] hits its horn, nail, or hoof, if it draws blood and reaches the flesh, it is permissible to eat it; otherwise no, because slaughter (tadhkiyah) is effective in the place of life. And if it cuts off other than the head and dies, the whole is eaten except what was cut off from the living, for that is dead and the ruling of slaughter does not appear on it. Not so if the head is cut off because the life of the body with separation of the head is inconceivable. And if a piece of skin hangs, if it would heal and become firm if left, it is permissible to eat it; otherwise it is separated. And if one cuts the game in half lengthwise and widthwise, it is permissible. And if one separates a part from the body, if it is less than half, the separated part is not permissible; if it is half, both are valid. End.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof discussing the permissibility of eating animals that cannot be slaughtered in the normal way. The matn states that tame game (an animal that was wild but became domesticated) is to be slaughtered normally, while wild cattle or those that have fallen into a well are to be killed by wounding (jarh). The commentary expands: if it is known that the animal died from the wound, it is halal; if known to have died from something else, it is haram; if uncertain, it is halal because the apparent cause is the wound. Similarly, a chicken stuck in a tree can be shot. The commentary then reports a difference from Imam Muhammad regarding sheep vs. cows/camels in urban vs. rural settings. The proof is the hadith of the runaway camel where the Prophet (SAW) allowed shooting it. The passage also includes rulings from al-Nawazil and al-Muhit on specific scenarios: a calf stuck in birth, hitting non-vital parts, severing parts less than half, etc. The key principle is that when normal slaughter is impossible, wounding becomes a valid substitute.

Key Terms
الجرح (al-jarḥ): Wounding an animal (e.g., by shooting) to kill it when normal slaughter is impossible.
العقر (al-'aqr): Shooting or wounding an animal to kill it, used interchangeably with jarh in this context.
الصائل (al-ṣā'il): An animal that attacks or becomes aggressive, treated like a runaway in terms of permissibility of shooting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a cow runs away in the city, is it permissible to eat it after shooting it?
A) Yes, because cows and camels are always permissible by shooting regardless of location.
B) No, because in the city one can catch it and slaughter normally.
C) Yes, but only if it runs away in the desert.
D) No, because shooting is never a valid method for cows.

Key Takeaway
Jarh is a valid substitute for slaughter when normal slaughter is impossible, provided the animal dies from the wound and the wound is effective.

Special Cases and Intra-Hanafi Differences on Jarh
Determines when jarh is valid substitute for slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Imam Muhammad's distinction regarding sheep versus cows/camels in urban and desert settings, and explain the rulings on cutting parts and hitting non-vital areas from al-Nawazil and al-Muhit.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on when jarh is valid, including distinctions between species and location, and on the consequences of cutting off parts of the animal.

This lesson delves into the more detailed rulings found in the passage, starting with Imam Muhammad's distinction between sheep and cows/camels when they run away in the city versus desert. Then we examine scenarios from later Hanafi works: a calf stuck in birth, hitting non-vital parts, severing a part of the animal, and cutting the animal in half. Understanding these nuances is crucial for applying the general principle correctly.

Guided Path
1
Study Imam Muhammad's distinction
Understand why sheep in the city are not permissible by shooting but in the desert are, and why cows/camels are always permissible. Note the basis: likelihood of capture.
2
Examine the sa'il ruling
How the aggressor is treated like a runaway, and the disagreement with Malik. This shows the expansion of the principle.
3
Analyze the birth scenario
The case of a cow with difficult birth: valid slaughter by hand if possible, otherwise wounding is permissible. This demonstrates the application of ajz in an emergency.
4
Evaluate rulings on hitting parts
What if an arrow hits the horn/hoof? Only halal if it draws blood and reaches flesh. This defines the condition of an effective wound.
5
Understand severing rulings
If a part is cut off, less than half is not halal, half or more is halal. Cutting the animal in half makes the whole halal. This shows how tadhkiyah applies to the body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وذبح صيد استأنس وجرح نعم توحش أو تردى في بئر) الواو عاطفة على قوله وحل ذبيحة مسلم وذبح صيد يعني وحل أكل صيد استأنس بالذبح وهو الاختيارية لقدرته عليها، وحل أكل نعم توحش أو تردى بالجرح لعجزه عن الاختيارية. هذا إذ علم أنه مات من الجرح، وإن علم أنه لم يمت من الجرح لم يؤكل» فإن أشكل ذلك أكل لأن الظاهر الموت به، وكذا الدجاجة إذا تعلقت على شجرة وخاف موتها صارت ذكاتها بالجرح وفي الكتاب أطلق فيما توحش من النعم وكذا فيما تردى فشمل ما إذا كان في المصر والصحراء، وعن محمد أن الشاة إذا ندت في المصر لا تحل بالعقر وإن ندت في الصحراء تحل بالعقر لتحقق العجز عن الذكاة الاختيارية وفي البقر والإبل يتحقق العجز سواء ندت في المصر أو في الصحراء فتحل بالعقر. والصائل كالناد إذا كان لا يقدر على أخذه حتى لو قتله المصول عليه وهو يريد ذكاته وسمى حل أكله خلافاً لمالك . ولنا ما روي منهم أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان في سفر فند بعير من الإبل ولم يكن معهم حبل فرماه رجل فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : إن لهذه البهائم أوابد كأوابد الوحش فما فعل منها فافعلوا به هكذا. رواه البخاري ومسلم ولأنه قد تحقق العجز عن الذكاة الاختيارية فصار إلى البدل. وفي النوازل : لو أن بقرة تعسر عليها الولادة فأدخل صاحبها يده وذبح الولد حل أكله، وإن جرحها في غير موضع الذبح إذا كان لا يقدر على ذبحه يحل وإن كان يقدر لا يحل اهـ. وفي المحيط : فإن أصاب قرنه أو ظفره أو حافره فإن أدماه ووصل للحم حل أكله وإلا فلا لأن الذكاة تصرف في محل الحياة وإن أبان عنه غير الرأس فمات يؤكل كله إلا ما أبان من الحي فهو ميت ولا يظهر فيه حكم الذكاة ولا كذلك إذا بان الرأس لأنه لا يتصور حياة الجسد مع إبانة الرأس. وإن تعلق منه جلدة فإن كان يلتئم ويتدبل لو تركه حل أكله وإلا فهو مبان، ولو قطع الصيد نصفين طولاً وعرضاً حل ولو أبان طائفة من الناس البدن إن كان أقل من النصف لا يحل المبان وإن كان النصف يصح كلاهما .اهـ.

الجرح (al-jarḥ): Wounding an animal (e.g., by shooting) to kill it when normal slaughter is impossible.

According to Imam Muhammad, if a sheep runs away in the city, is it permissible to eat it after shooting?

Key Takeaway

Sunnah Method: Nahr for Camels, Dhabh for Others
Clarifies the sunnah method of slaughter and its wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method of slaughter for camels, cows, and sheep, and explain why the opposite is disliked.

Core Idea
Slaughter camels by nahr (low neck), others by dhabh (upper neck) – opposite is valid but disliked.

The etiquettes of slaughter (dhabh) are part of the sunnah, and the method recommended by the Prophet varies by animal. In this passage, we learn that camels should be sacrificed by nahr, while cows and sheep by dhabh, based on transmitted practice and ease. We also explore the definitions and postures along with the permissibility of any part of the throat.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify what the matn says: it is sunnah to do nahr for camels and dhabh for cows/sheep, and the opposite is disliked.
The ruling is on the preferred method, not on validity.
2
Identify the evidence
The text cites Quranic verses (Al-Baqarah 2:67, Al-Kawthar 108:2) and the prophetic practice as the basis.
The verse 'And sacrifice' is interpreted as nahr of the camel.
3
Understand definitions
Nahr cuts the lower neck near the chest; dhabh cuts the upper neck below the jawbones.
These are the key terms.
4
Note sunnah postures
From al-Jami' al-Saghir: nahr is performed standing, dhabh with the animal lying down.
This adds practical detail.
5
Recognize throat permissibility
Any part of the throat (halq) from labbah to jawbones is valid for dhabh because veins are present throughout.
This does not contradict the specification of nahr for camels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وسن نحر الإبل وذبح البقر والغنم وكره عكسه وحل وإنما كان هذا الفعل مسنوناً لأنه هو المنقول عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال الله تعالى إن الله يأمركم أن تذبحوا بقرة ﴾ [البقرة: ٦٧] وقال تعالى فصل لربك وانحر﴾ [الكوثر : ٢] قالوا المراد نحر الجزور وفي البقر والغنم الذبح أيسر، وفي الإبل النحر أيسر وإنما كره العكس لترك السنة. والنحر قطع العروق في أسفل العنق عند الصدر، والذبح قطع العروق من أعلى العنق تحت اللحيين. وفي الجامع الصغير : والسنة في النحر أن ينحر قائماً. وفي الشاة والبقر أن تذبح مضطجعة اهـ. وفيه أيضاً: ولا بأس بالذبح في الحلق كله أسفله وأوسطه وأعلاه لأن ما بين اللبة واللحيين وهو الحلق ولأن كله مجتمع العروق فصار حكم الكل واحداً فإن قلت هذا ينافي في ما تقدم من التقييد قلنا : لا لأن النحر في أسفله.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is a sunnah to sacrifice camels by nahr, and to slaughter cows and sheep by dhabh, and its opposite is disliked, and [the meat] is permissible.) And this action is only sunnah because it is what is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. Allah Most High said: 'Indeed Allah commands you to slaughter a cow' [Al-Baqarah: 67], and He said: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' [Al-Kawthar: 2]. They said: the intended meaning is the sacrifice of the camel. And in cows and sheep, dhabh is easier, and in camels, nahr is easier. And the opposite is only disliked because of abandoning the sunnah. And nahr is the cutting of the veins in the lower part of the neck near the chest, and dhabh is the cutting of the veins from the upper part of the neck below the jawbones. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: The sunnah in nahr is to sacrifice while standing, and in sheep and cows, to slaughter while lying down. End. And in it also: There is no harm in slaughtering in any part of the throat (halq): its lower, middle, or upper part, because what is between the hollow of the throat (labbah) and the jawbones is the throat, and because all of it contains the veins, so the ruling of the whole is one. If you say: this contradicts the previous restriction, we say: No, because nahr is in its lower part [of the throat].
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement clarifying the sunnah method for slaughter. The matn states that it is sunnah to sacrifice camels by nahr (cutting the throat at the lower part near the chest) and to slaughter cows and sheep by dhabh (cutting the upper throat below the jaw). Doing the opposite is disliked. The commentary explains that this is sunnah because it is the transmitted practice of the Prophet (SAW) and is easier for each type of animal. The verse from al-Kawthar is interpreted as referring to the nahr of the camel. The commentary then gives definitions: nahr is cutting the veins at the lower neck; dhabh is cutting the upper neck. It also quotes al-Jami' al-Saghir: the sunnah for nahr is to stand, for dhabh to lay the animal down. Additionally, it states that any part of the throat (from the hollow to the jaw) is permissible for dhabh, as all contain the veins. This does not contradict the specificity of nahr because nahr is specifically the lower part.

Key Terms
النحر (al-naḥr): Slaughtering by cutting the veins at the lower part of the neck near the chest, specifically for camels.
الذبح (al-dhabḥ): Slaughtering by cutting the veins from the upper part of the neck below the jawbones, the standard method for most animals.
الحلق (al-ḥalq): The throat area from the hollow of the throat (labbah) to the jawbones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the sunnah method for slaughtering a cow?
A) Nahr (cut at the lower neck) while standing.
B) Dhabh (cut at the upper neck) while lying down.
C) Either nahr or dhabh with no preference.
D) Dhabh while standing.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah method varies by animal: nahr for camels, dhabh for others; opposite is valid but disliked.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Fetus and the Mother's Slaughter
Intra-Hanafi dispute: positions and proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the fetus ruling, identify the proofs for each, and determine the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A fetus found in a slaughtered animal: Abu Hanifa says haram without separate slaughter; the Sahibayn say halal by the mother's slaughter.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on a practical question: if you slaughter a pregnant animal, can you eat the fetus without slaughtering it separately? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the fetus is not made permissible by the mother's slaughter, while his two principal disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that it is. Understanding this dispute reveals how different proofs (Quran, hadith, and analogy) are weighed within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions clearly
Identify which imams hold that the fetus is not permissible (Abu Hanifa, Zufar, al-Hasan) and which hold it is permissible (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and a group). Note the condition: 'if its creation is completed' (fully formed).
2
Analyse the proofs of the Sahibayn
Examine the two hadith proofs: (1) 'The slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother' (general principle). (2) The incident where the Prophet explicitly allowed eating the fetus. Also the analogy: the fetus is part of the mother in reality and rulings.
3
Analyse the proof of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa relies on the Quranic verse forbidding carrion (al-maytah). He argues the fetus dies its own death (by the mother's slaughter, not directly), so it falls under the prohibition.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Later Hanafi authorities, such as al-Marghinani, affirmed this as the relied-upon view.
5
Apply the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one follows Abu Hanifa, the fetus must be slaughtered separately to be halal. If one follows the Sahibayn, it is halal to eat without separate slaughter, provided it is fully formed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ولم يذك جنين بذكاة أمه) يعني مذكى بذكاة أمه حتى لا يحل أكله بذكاتها وهذا عند الإمام وزفر والحسن رحمهما الله تعالى. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد وجماعة أخر: إذا تم خلقه حل أكله بذكاتها لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «ذكاة الجنين ذكاة أمه» (۱) ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لما قيل له إنا ننحر الناقة ونذبح الشاة وفي بطنها الجنين أنلقيه أم نأكله؟ قال : كله إن شئت فإن ذكاته ذكاة أمه. ولأنه جزء من حقيقة لكونه متصلاً بها وحكماً حتى يدخل في الأحكام الواردة على الأم من البيع والهبة والعتق وللإمام قوله تعالى إنما حرم عليكم الميتة [البقرة : ١٧٣] وهو اسم لحيوان مات من غير ذكاة والجنين مات حتف أنفه فيحرم بالكتاب. ويكره ذبح الشاة إذا
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the fetus is not made permissible by the slaughter of its mother.) Meaning: it is not made permissible by the slaughter of its mother, so it is not permissible to eat it by her slaughter. This is according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], Zufar, and al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on them. And Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and other groups said: If its creation is completed, it is permissible to eat it by her slaughter because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother.' And because of his saying, peace be upon him, when it was said to him: 'We sacrifice the camel and slaughter the sheep, and in its belly is a fetus; shall we throw it away or eat it?' He said: 'Eat it if you wish, for its slaughter is the slaughter of its mother.' And because it is a part of the reality [of the mother] due to its being connected to her, and a part in ruling, so that it enters into the rulings that apply to the mother, such as sale, gift, and manumission. And for the Imam [Abu Hanifa] is the saying of Allah Most High: 'He has only forbidden to you carrion' [Al-Baqarah: 173], which is a name for an animal that dies without slaughter, and the fetus died by its own death, so it is forbidden by the Book. And it is disliked to slaughter the sheep if...
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, Zufar, and al-Hasan: the fetus is not made permissible by the mother's slaughter; it must be slaughtered separately. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and other scholars hold that if the fetus is fully formed, it is permissible to eat it by the mother's slaughter. They provide two hadith proofs: (1) 'The slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother'; (2) The Prophet's explicit permission to eat a fetus found in a slaughtered animal. They also argue by analogy: the fetus is part of the mother in reality and in rulings. Abu Hanifa's proof is the Quranic verse forbidding carrion (al-maytah), arguing that the fetus dies its own death and thus falls under that prohibition. The passage ends mid-sentence about a disliked action, but the core dispute is complete. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, i.e., the fetus is permissible if fully formed.

Key Terms
الجنين (al-janīn): The fetus of an animal; its ruling when found in a slaughtered mother is disputed.
ذكاة الأم (dhakāt al-umm): The slaughter of the mother; whether it extends to the fetus.
الميتة (al-maytah): Carrion: an animal that died without proper slaughter; used by Abu Hanifa to argue fetus is forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi madhhab regarding a fully formed fetus found in a slaughtered animal?
A) It is not permissible because it died its own death.
B) It is permissible to eat without separate slaughter.
C) It is permissible only if the mother was slaughtered facing the qiblah.
D) It is not permissible unless the fetus was alive at the moment of slaughter.

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that a fully formed fetus found in a slaughtered animal is permissible to eat without separate slaughter, based on the Prophet's explicit permission.

The Sunnah Method of Slaughter: Nahr for Camels, Dhabh for Others
Explaining the sunnah and definition of nahr and dhabh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method of slaughter for camels, cows, and sheep, and explain why reversal is makruh but the meat remains halal.

Core Idea
Slaughter method is sunnah-specific: nahr for camels, dhabh for cows/sheep; reversal is makruh but not haram.

The proper method of slaughter (dhabh) is a crucial part of meat consumption in Islam. This lesson clarifies the recommended (sunnah) method for different animals according to the Hanafi school, distinguishing between nahr for camels and dhabh for cows and sheep. We will explore the textual proof and the legal reasoning behind this distinction, as well as the definition of each term and the rulings when the sunnah is reversed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its sunnah ruling
The passage states that it is sunnah to nahr camels and to dhabh cows and sheep. Identify the specific animal and the prescribed method.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quranic verses (Al-Baqarah 2:67 and Al-Kawthar 108:2) and a hadith about a camel escaping. Note how these proofs establish the method.
The hadith shows a substitute when ideal slaughter is impossible.
3
Understand the definitions
Nahr is defined as cutting the veins at the bottom of the neck near the chest; dhabh is cutting the veins from the upper neck under the jaw. Learn the precise locations.
The difference is the site of incision.
4
Note the ruling on reversal
Reversing the method (e.g., dhabh for a camel) is makruh tanzihi (disliked) but the meat remains halal. Understand the basis: leaving the sunnah.
Dislike is due to abandoning the transmitted practice.
5
Explore the scope of permissibility
In case of inability, substitutes are allowed (e.g., shooting a runaway camel). Also note edge cases like the fetus or wounds from the hadith and ancillary texts.
The principle of 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الذبائح الإبل وذبح البقر والغنم وكره عكسه وحل ولم يذك جنين بذكاة أمه . منهم أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان في سفر فند بعير من الإبل ولم يكن معهم حبل فرماه رجل فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : إن لهذه البهائم أوابد كأوابد الوحش فما فعل منها فافعلوا به هكذا. رواه البخاري ومسلم ولأنه قد تحقق العجز عن الذكاة الاختيارية فصار إلى البدل. وفي النوازل : لو أن بقرة تعسر عليها الولادة فأدخل صاحبها يده وذبح الولد حل أكله، وإن جرحها في غير موضع الذبح إذا كان لا يقدر على ذبحه يحل وإن كان يقدر لا يحل اهـ. وفي المحيط : فإن أصاب قرنه أو ظفره أو حافره فإن أدماه ووصل للحم حل أكله وإلا فلا لأن الذكاة تصرف في محل الحياة وإن أبان عنه غير الرأس فمات يؤكل كله إلا ما أبان عن الحي فهو ميت ولا يظهر فيه حكم الذكاة ولا كذلك إذا بان الرأس لأنه لا يتصور حياة الجسد مع إبانة الرأس. وإن تعلق منه جلدة فإن كان يلتئم ويتدبل لو تركه حل أكله وإلا فهو مبان، ولو قطع الصيد نصفين طولاً وعرضاً حل ولو أبان طائفة من الناس البدن إن كان أقل . من النصف لا يحل ،المبان، وإن كان النصف يصح كلاهما .اهـ. قال رحمه الله : (وسن نحر الإبل وذبح البقر والغنم وكره عكسه وحل وإنما كان هذا الفعل مسنوناً لأنه هو المنقول عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال الله تعالى إن الله يأمركم أن تذبحوا بقرة ﴾ [البقرة: ٦٧] وقال تعالى فصل لربك وانحر﴾ [الكوثر : ٢] قالوا المراد نحر الجزور وفي البقر والغنم الذبح أيسر، وفي الإبل النحر أيسر وإنما كره العكس لترك السنة. والنحر قطع العروق في أسفل العنق عند الصدر، والذبح قطع العروق من أعلى العنق تحت اللحيين. وفي الجامع الصغير : والسنة في النحر أن ينحر قائماً. وفي الشاة والبقر أن تذبح مضطجعة اهـ. وفيه أيضاً: ولا بأس بالذبح في الحلق كله أسفله وأوسطه وأعلاه لأن ما بين اللبة واللحيين وهو الحلق ولأن كله مجتمع العروق فصار حكم الكل واحداً فإن قلت هذا ينافي في ما تقدم من التقييد قلنا : لا لأن النحر في أسفله.
Book of Slaughter. Camels, slaughter of cows and sheep, disliked is its opposite, and (it is) permissible. And the fetus is not made lawful by the slaughter of its mother. Among them: that the Prophet was in a journey and a camel escaped, and they had no rope, so a man shot it with an arrow, and the Prophet said: 'These beasts have habits like wild animals, so if one of them does that, treat it like this.' Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. And because inability for ideal slaughter is confirmed, so one resorts to the substitute. In al-Nawazil: If a cow has difficulty giving birth and her owner inserts his hand and slaughters the offspring, it is halal; and if he wounds it in a non-slaughter place, if he could not slaughter it, it is halal; but if he could, it is not halal. In al-Muhit: If (a bullet) hits its horn, nail, or hoof, and it bleeds and reaches the flesh, it is halal; otherwise no, because slaughter affects the seat of life. And if he severs something other than the head and it dies, all is eaten except the severed part from the living, which is dead. Not so if the head is severed. And if a skin hangs, if it would heal and dry if left, it is halal; otherwise it is severed. And if one cuts the game into two halves lengthwise and breadthwise, it is halal. And if one severs a portion of the body, if less than half, the severed part is not halal; if half, both are fine. He said: 'And it is sunnah to nahr camels and to slaughter cows and sheep, and its opposite is disliked, and it is permissible.' This act is sunnah because it is transmitted from the Prophet. Allah said: 'Allah commands you to slaughter a cow' (2:67) and 'Pray to your Lord and sacrifice (nahr)' (108:2). They said the intent is nahr of the camel; for cows and sheep, slaughter is easier; for camels, nahr is easier. The dislike of the opposite is due to leaving the sunnah. Nahr is cutting the veins in the lower part of the neck at the chest; slaughter is cutting the veins from the upper neck under the jaw. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: And the sunnah in nahr is to do it standing; for sheep and cows, to slaughter them lying on the side. Also in it: There is no harm in slaughtering in any part of the throat, its lower, middle, and upper, because the area between the pit of the throat and the jaws is the throat, and all of it contains the veins, so the ruling is the same. If you say this contradicts the earlier restriction, we say no, because nahr is in its lower part.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage begins the Book of Slaughter (Kitab al-Dhaba'ih) by explaining the sunnah method of slaughtering different animals. The matn (text) states: 'It is sunnah to nahr camels and to dhabh cows and sheep; its opposite is makruh; and it is permissible. And the fetus is not made lawful by the slaughter of its mother.' The commentary first addresses the ruling on the method of slaughter. The author provides a hadith proof: the Prophet allowed shooting a camel that ran away, indicating that when one cannot perform the ideal slaughter, a substitute is permissible. Then the author quotes Quranic verses: 'Allah commands you to slaughter a cow' (2:67) and 'Pray to your Lord and sacrifice (nahr)' (108:2), establishing the basis. He then defines nahr as cutting the veins at the bottom of the neck near the chest, and dhabh as cutting the veins from the upper neck under the jaw. The sunnah for nahr is to do it while standing; for sheep and cows, while lying on the side. It is also permissible to slaughter anywhere in the throat (halq) because the veins are all there, but nahr is specifically at the lower end. The dislike (karahah) of reversing the method is because it abandons the sunnah.

Key Terms
النحر (al-nahr): Cutting the veins at the bottom of the neck near the chest, as prescribed for camels.
الذبح (al-dhabh): Cutting the veins from the upper neck under the jaw, as prescribed for cows and sheep.
السنة (al-sunnah): A recommended practice established by the Prophet's deed or approval; leaving it is makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on reversing the sunnah method (e.g., dhabh for a camel) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Haram, the meat is unlawful
B) Makruh tanzihi, but the meat is halal
C) Mubah, no issue
D) Sunnah as well, equally recommended

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes nahr for camels and dhabh for cows and sheep as sunnah; reversal is makruh but the meat remains halal.

Ruling on the Fetus (Janeen) Being Lawful through the Mother's Slaughter
Explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the fetus is made lawful by the mother's slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-school dispute on the fetus being made lawful by the mother's slaughter, explain the proofs of each side, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the positions.

Core Idea
The fetus is not automatically halal by the mother's slaughter according to Abu Hanifa; it requires its own separate slaughter.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi dispute: when a pregnant animal is slaughtered, does the fetus become halal? The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq adopts Imam Abu Hanifa's strict position, but his two eminent disciples disagreed. We will explore the textual proofs and the practical consequences of each view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify which view is taken by Abu Hanifa and which by the Sahibayn. Note the scholars supporting each side.
Abu Hanifa is joined by Zufar and Hasan.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Analyze the Quranic verse 'He has only forbidden you dead animals' (2:173). Understand how the fetus qualifies as maytah.
The fetus dies without direct slaughter.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Review the hadith 'The slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother' and the practical hadith. Consider the logical argument that the fetus is part of the mother's body.
These proofs indicate the mother's slaughter suffices.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how Abu Hanifa counters the hadith: either it is interpreted for a live fetus or abrogated. The Quranic general ruling takes precedence.
This is a classic clash of 'amm and khass.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: if a fully formed fetus is found, Abu Hanifa says it is haram unless separately slaughtered; the Sahibayn say it is halal as is.
This affects actual consumption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولم يذك جنين بذكاة أمه) يعني مذكى بذكاة أمه حتى لا يحل أكله بذكاتها وهذا عند الإمام وزفر والحسن رحمهما الله تعالى. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد وجماعة أخر: إذا تم خلقه حل أكله بذكاتها لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «ذكاة الجنين ذكاة أمه» (۱) ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لما قيل له إنا ننحر الناقة ونذبح الشاة وفي بطنها الجنين أنلقيه أم نأكله؟ قال : كله إن شئت فإن ذكاته ذكاة أمه. ولأنه جزء من حقيقة لكونه متصلاً بها وحكماً حتى يدخل في الأحكام الواردة على الأم من البيع والهبة والعتق وللإمام قوله تعالى إنما حرم عليكم الميتة [البقرة : ١٧٣] وهو اسم لحيوان مات من غير ذكاة والجنين مات حتف أنفه فيحرم بالكتاب. ويكره ذبح الشاة إذا تقارب ولادتها لأنه يضيع ما في بطنها. الدجاجة إذا تعلقت فرماها وأصابها ينظر؛ إن كان لا يهتدي إلى منزله حل أكله لأنه عجز عن الذكاة الاختيارية وإن كان يهتدي ذكر الفقيه أبو الليث إن أصاب المذبح حل وإن أصاب غيره فعند محمد يحل وعن غيره يحل اهـ. والله تعالى أعلم .
He said: 'And the fetus is not made lawful by the slaughter of its mother.' Meaning it is not considered slaughtered by its mother's slaughter, so it is not permissible to eat it by her slaughter. This is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), Zufar, and Hasan. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and other scholars said: If its creation is complete, then eating it is lawful by her slaughter, due to his statement: 'The slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother,' and due to his statement when it was said to him: 'We slaughter the she-camel and the sheep and in its belly is a fetus, should we throw it or eat it?' He said: 'Eat it if you wish, for its slaughter is the slaughter of its mother.' And because it is a part of her reality and ruling, so it enters into the rulings of sale, gift, and manumission that apply to the mother. And for Imam (Abu Hanifa) is the statement of Allah: 'He has only forbidden you dead animals' (2:173), which is a name for an animal that died without slaughter, and the fetus dies of itself, so it is forbidden by the Book. And it is disliked to slaughter a sheep when her giving birth is near because it wastes what is in her belly. Regarding a chicken if it becomes attached and one shoots it and hits it, one looks: if he cannot find his way to its home, it is halal because of inability for ideal slaughter; if he can find his way, al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned that if he hits the slaughter spot it is halal, if he hits elsewhere, according to Muhammad it is halal, and according to others it is halal. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the status of a fetus found in the womb of a slaughtered animal. The matn states that the fetus is not made lawful by the mother's slaughter. The commentary clarifies that this is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, Zufar, and Hasan. They argue based on the Quranic prohibition of dead animals (al-maytah), since the fetus dies in the womb without direct slaughter. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if the fetus is fully formed, it is lawful to eat it by virtue of the mother's slaughter. They cite the hadith 'The slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother' and another hadith where the Prophet permitted eating the fetus from a slaughtered animal. They also reason that the fetus is part of the mother's body and shares her rulings in sale, gift, and manumission. The passage also adds that it is disliked to slaughter a sheep close to giving birth because it wastes the fetus, and if a chicken is shot and cannot be reached, it may be eaten if the hunter lost its way.

Key Terms
جنين (janeen): Unborn offspring of an animal in the womb.
ذكاة (dhakah): Slaughter according to Islamic law; making an animal halal by cutting the throat.
ميتة (maytah): An animal that died without proper Islamic slaughter; forbidden to eat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on eating a fetus found fully formed in the belly of a slaughtered animal?
A) It is halal without further slaughter.
B) It is haram unless it is also slaughtered separately.
C) It is halal only if it moves after the mother's slaughter.
D) It is makruh but permissible.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the fetus is not automatically halal by the mother's slaughter according to Imam Abu Hanifa; separate slaughter is required.

Prohibition of Magpie, Bat, Hyena, Insects, Donkeys, and Mules
Enumerates the prohibition of several animals with Quran and hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of these animals and cite the Quranic or hadith proof that establishes the prohibition.

Core Idea
Predators, carrion-eaters, and vile creatures are haram by the Quranic prohibition of 'khaba'ith', while donkeys and mules are haram by explicit hadith.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on several animals whose permissibility is questioned. The author uses the general Quranic principle of 'khaba'ith' (vile things) and specific hadith prohibitions to declare these animals unlawful. Understanding these rulings requires careful application of textual evidence and awareness of internal Hanafi differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify each animal and its initial ruling
List the animals mentioned: magpie, bat, hyena, insects (lizard, wasp, turtle), domestic donkey, and mule. Note the initial ruling from the text.
Some animals have internal differences (magpie, bat).
2
Locate the primary proof for each animal
For magpie: it eats chickens (predator). For bat: has fang. For hyena: eats carrion. For insects: general classification as khubuth (Quran 7:157). For donkey: explicit hadith prohibition (Bukhari). For mule: analogy to donkey with nuance for horse mother.
The Quranic verse on khubuth is a broad proof.
3
Understand the chronological refinement of prohibitions
The text clarifies that the verse in Surah al-An'am (6:145) initially only prohibited three things, but later Allah prohibited khaba'ith through other verses. Thus early reports of permissibility are abrogated.
This resolves seeming contradictions in revealed texts.
4
Resolve internal Hanafi differences
For magpie, Imam Abu Yusuf considered it makruh due to carrion eating, but the first opinion (probably Abu Hanifa) prohibited it because it eats chickens; the text prefers the prohibition. For bat, two narrations exist; the text decides it is not eaten due to fang.
The preferred view for both is prohibition.
5
Determine the mufta bihi for each
Magpie: haram (first opinion preferred). Bat: haram. Hyena: haram. Insects: haram. Donkey: haram. Mule: haram (if mother is donkey; if mother is horse, see horse ruling).
All are haram, except possibly magpie if one follows Abu Yusuf's weaker view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأرنب وذبح ما لا يؤكل لحمه يطهر لحمه وجلده إلا الآدمي والخنزير ولا يؤكل مائي الإمام وهو العقعق لأنه يأكل الدجاج. وعن أبي يوسف أنه يكره أكله لأنه غالب أكله الجيف والأول أصح. قال في النهاية : ذكر في بعض المواضع أن الخفاش يؤكل، وذكر في بعضها أنه لا يؤكل لأن له ناباً . وأما الضبع فلما روينا وبينا ولأنه يؤكل الجيف فيكون لحمه خبيئاً. وأما الضب والزنبور والسلحفاة والحشرات فلأنها من الخبائث وقد قال تعالى ويحرم عليكم الخبائث) [الأعراف : ١٥٧] وما روي من الإباحة محمول على ما قبل التحريم ثم حرم الخبائث لأنه لم يكن محرماً في الابتداء إلا ثلاثة أشياء على ما قال الله تعالى قل لا أجد فيما أوحي إلي محرما [الأنعام: ١٤٥] إلى آخر الآية . ثم حرم بعد ذلك أشياء . وأما الحمر الأهلية فلما روى البخاري رحمه الله تعالى حرم رسول الله له و لحوم الحمر الأهلية. وأما البغل فلأنه من نسل الحمار فكان كأصله حتى لو كانت أمه فرساً فعلى الخلاف المعروف في الخيل لأن المعتبر هو الأم. قال رحمه الله : وحل الأرنب لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر أصحابه أن يأكلوه حين أهدي إليه مشوياً. رواه أحمد والنسائي. ولأنه ليس من السباع ولا يؤكل الجيف فأشبه الظبي.
The rabbit, and slaughtering what is not eaten for meat purifies its meat and its skin except the human and the pig. And the aquatic [animal] of the Imam is not eaten, and it is the magpie because it eats chickens. And from Abu Yusuf that he dislikes eating it because most of its food is carrion, and the first is more correct. He said in al-Nihaya: It is mentioned in some places that the bat is eaten, and mentioned in some that it is not eaten because it has a fang. As for the hyena, due to what we have narrated and clarified, and because it eats carrion, so its meat is vile. As for the lizard, the wasp, the turtle, and the insects, they are from the vile things, and Allah has said: 'And prohibits for them the vile things' [al-A'raf:157]. And what is narrated of permissibility is carried upon [the period] before prohibition, then He prohibited vile things because at the beginning nothing was prohibited except three things according to what Allah said: 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything prohibited' [al-An'am:145] to the end of the verse. Then afterwards He prohibited things. As for domestic donkeys, because al-Bukhari related that the Messenger of Allah prohibited their meat. As for the mule, because it is from the offspring of the donkey, so it is like its origin, such that if its mother is a horse, then there is the well-known difference of opinion regarding horses because the consideration is the mother. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: And the rabbit is lawful because the Prophet, peace be upon him, ordered his companions to eat it when it was presented to him roasted. Ahmad and al-Nasa'i narrated it. And because it is not from the predators and does not eat carrion, so it resembles the deer.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs concerning the permissibility and prohibition of various animals. The commentator begins by stating the rabbit's ruling and the general principle that slaughtering an animal not eaten for meat purifies its meat and skin, except human and pig. He then lists several animals: the magpie is not eaten because it eats chickens, though Abu Yusuf considers it disliked; bat is disputed due to its fang; hyena is forbidden because it eats carrion; lizard, wasp, turtle, and insects are forbidden as 'vile things' based on Quran 7:157. Domestic donkeys are forbidden by explicit hadith prohibition. Mules follow the ruling of donkeys, but if the mother is a horse, there is a known disagreement regarding horses, as the mother's species is considered. Finally, rabbit is explicitly permitted by the Prophet's command and analogy to deer, as it is not a predator.

Key Terms
خبائث (khabā'ith): Vile, impure things that are detestable and prohibited by the Quran.
جيف (jiyaf): Carrion, dead animals not slaughtered properly.
ذبائح (dhabā'iḥ): The chapter on slaughtering, covering rulings on animals that are slaughtered and their permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this lesson, what is the ruling on eating magpie?
A) Halal
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Predators and carrion-eaters are haram by the Quranic prohibition of khaba'ith; domestic donkeys are haram by hadith; mules follow the same ruling.

Purification by Slaughtering Animals Not Eaten for Meat
States a general principle regarding purification through slaughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that slaughtering an animal whose meat is not eaten purifies its meat and skin, and identify the exceptions.

Core Idea
Slaughtering an inedible animal renders its meat and skin pure, except for human and pig, which are never purified by slaughter.

This lesson focuses on a specific ruling from the beginning of the passage: slaughtering an animal that is not eaten for meat nonetheless purifies its meat and skin. This is a unique Hanafi principle. The exceptions are human and pig. Understanding this helps in dealing with the products of such animals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering (dhabh) an animal that is not permissible to eat (e.g., donkey, mule, predatory birds). The ruling is that the meat and skin become pure (tahir).
This does not make the meat halal to eat; it only removes the impurity of unslaughtered carrion.
2
Note the exceptions: human and pig
The text excludes human and pig. Their meat and skin are not purified by slaughter. Human is not slaughtered; pig is impure even when slaughtered.
This is consistent with the Quranic prohibition of pork and the sanctity of human remains.
3
Understand the purpose of this ruling
Even though the meat is not eaten, its slaughter prevents it from being considered carrion (maytah) and allows beneficial use of the skin (e.g., for leather) and possibly other parts.
This is a practical ruling for animals that are not food but can be used for their hides or other products.
